As of March 2025, the construction of the early works is underway as follows.
     •    Access road to the HPP site: 2.5km out of 5.6km has been laid with concrete with overall progress at
          22.32%.
     •    Bridge over the Naryn River: Foundation and piling works for pillars 1–4 are in progress. However,
          due to cold weather and rising water levels, construction has been suspended since December 12,
          2024
     •    Transport tunnel: The 126-meter Transport Tunnel TT-2 has been fully excavated (100%), with road
          leveling and concreting currently in progress.
     •    110kV Overhead transmission line tower and substation: 6.794 km (37.7%) of the transmission line
          has been completed, with 25 poles and 732 insulators installed.
In terms of land ownership, the area considered under this consultancy is state -owned but the user
rights to the area have been transferred since 2012 and 2013 to the Electric Power Plants Open
Joint Stock Company.

3. Objectives of Consultancy Services
The task required is to prepare a Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Plan for the construction
site and associated facilities of the K1-HPP Project (LRRP1). The LRRP1 preparation must be compliant
with the Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework (LRRF) of the Project, international
social standards such as Environmental and Social Framework from the World Bank (WB), the
Environmental and Social Framework of the Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB), the
European Investment Bank (EIB)’s Environmental and Social Sustainability Framework, the European
Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD)’s Environmental and Social Performance
Requirements and the Kyrgyz Republic’s relevant laws and regulations. The document must comply
with the requirements of the WB’s ESS5.

4. Scope of Works
The Consultant’s tasks shall include, but not be limited to, the following:
     •    Prepare an inception report detailing the methodology used to prepare the LRRP1. This inception
          report will be submitted to K1-PMO and the WB for approval.
     •    For the DDR: Conduct due diligence review to what extent land acquisition and restrictions on land
          use conducted for the early works and associated facilities were carried out in compliance with the
          principles of ESS5 and the regulations of the Kyrgyz Republic. It will include a Corrective Action Plan
          with timelines, responsibilities, and budget.
     •    For the preparation of the LRRP1:
                o    Update the social screening conducted in 2025 by the K1 ESIA consultant (SMEC) , covering,
                     among others, the rapid preliminary assessment to collect information on proposed land
                     location, area, ownership details, current land use, tenure status of present land use and unit
                     of government having jurisdiction on land.
                o    Carry out a census (including establishing a cut-off date) and inventory of loss (IOL) to
                     identify the persons who will be affected by the Project, to establish an inventory of land and
                     assets to be affected, to determine who will be eligible for compensation and assistance, and
                     to discourage ineligible persons, such as opportunistic settlers, from claiming benefits. The
                     exercise will be conducted using a structured questionnaire. The consultant will develop a
                     database of physical quantities of impacts and lay down the basis for developing an
                     entitlement policy and compensation package.




                                                                                                                                 Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



              o   Conduct a socio-economic survey (SES) to establish baseline data for use in the description of
                  PAPs, provide a basis for the design of, and budgeting for, the resettlement program, and
                  inform baseline for monitoring and evaluation of land acquisition, compensation, assistance,
                  and resettlement of the Project.
              o   Deliver a GIS-compatible database of affected assets and affected people capturing
                  information gathered in SES and IOL, the structure of which will be agreed with the K1 PMO
                  and the Government of Kyrgyz Republic (GoKR) prior to survey inception, and which will be
                  designed upfront to evolve and be used in further steps (LRRP1 implementation) as the main
                  database for compensation administration (preparation of compensation agreements) and
                  livelihood restoration monitoring.
              o   Conduct a Replacement Costs Survey (RCS) on affected land and non-land assets (if any).
                  The RCS will need to be carried out to establish the basis for calculation of replacement costs
                  for all the lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project. In relation to this, RCS needs
                  to be completed to establish compensation rates for the LRRP1. The consultant will calculate
                  the cost of compensation, assistance, and resettlement based on the RCS results and the
                  Entitlement Matrix approved as part of LRRF.
              o   Conduct and document consultations with PAPs, local authorities, Non-government
                  Organizations (NGOs) and relevant stakeholder through public consultation meetings, focus
                  group discussions (FGDs), key-informant interviews (KIIs), and in-depth face-to-face
                  interviews in Kyrgyz or Russian language to ascertain their opinions, concerns about various
                  aspects of land acquisition, in particular entitlements on compensation, assistance, and
                  resettlement, replacement pasture, restoration of loss of access to pastureland and livelihood
                  restoration. Take the opinions and concerns into account and ensure they are addressed and
                  incorporated into the LRRP1.
              o   Consultations with women and vulnerable group, in particular, will be carried out to
                  understand their specific concerns and views. Based on the outcome of these consultations, if
                  required, suitable mitigation measures will be incorporated into the Project and LRRP1.
              o   Prepare a LRRP1 for construction site and associated facilities based on the outcome of the
                  IOL, SES, RCS, due diligence findings, ESIA and the LRRF. The LRRP1 will also include
                  entitlements for different types of impacts, socio economic characteristics of the affected
                  persons, corrective actions for land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement
                  for associated facilities, institutional mechanisms, implementation schedules, budgets,
                  grievance redress mechanism, coordination of implementation in conjunction with civil works
                  procurement and construction schedules and monitoring mechanisms. The LRRP will comply
                  with the principles outlined in the LRRF and the WB’s ESS5. The outline of the LRRP1 is
                  attached in Appendix 1.

5. Specific Tasks for the preparation of the LRRP1
5.1 Census and Inventory of Losses
The census and IOL shall be carried out for 100% of the affected households using a structured
questionnaire to record the details of the affected persons. The exercise will help to: (i) obtain a full
inventory of affected assets that will support the determination of compensation for each and
every of these assets; (ii) prevent further influx of persons within the identified project area; (iii)
Assess the magnitude of impact to private assets and livelihoods; and (iv) Assess the extent of
physical and/or economic displacement. The census and the IOL will be based on the preliminary
design included in the feasibility study. It is important to cover all people adversely affected by the
construction site and associated facilities, regardless of their legal status – landowners, land users,
holders of land rights, tenants, illegal squatter – or whether they are actually living on the affected
site at the time of the census and IOL. In other words, private landowners and holders of rights to
land as well as any person currently occupying public or private land for shelter, business purposes,
or other sources of livelihood should be included in the census and IOL.




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



The consultant is asked to identify the persons who will be affected by the Project, and establish an
inventory of land and assets to be affected following the steps below:
    (i)     Develop a structured questionnaire for review and approval by K1-PMO and World Bank.
    (ii)    Approach the Municipal Enterprises and those in charge of land management who holds the land
            records to collect (or purchase) of cadastral maps/land use maps on the project villages and AAs.
    (iii)   Overlay the map of the construction site and associated facilities on the land use maps of the relevant
            AAs. This method will provide basic information such as types of affected lands; amounts of affected
            lands; number of the plots, etc. The consultant will review of cadastral records together with the
            Municipal Enterprises and land management officers and village and AA leaders.
    (iv)    Lay-out the area required for construction site and associated facilities on the ground with support of
            a design engineer, representatives from Municipal Enterprises, village leaders/AA leaders and GPS,
            the consultant will identify the location of the Project area in the field and identify the impacts due to
            construction site preparation and construction of associated facilities;
    (v)     Together with village leaders and Municipal Enterprises of affected AAs to identify the affected
            households and conduct interviews with household heads or their spouses using the questionnaire to
            determine their scope of land acquisition impacts.
    (vi)    Take photos of affected households (the heads of household - husband and wife - or with many
            household members as possible) with their household ID in front of their affected house/land,
            previous written permission provided. All the affected land and assets should be photographed along
            with GIS coordinates.
    (vii) Analyse the data on the land acquisition impacts.
•           All the IOL information must be geo-referenced.
The following data and information need to be collected during the IOL, but not limited to:
      (i)       Affected assets that need to be enumerated for each project component;
      •     Private land (agricultural land, etc.) that will be permanently acquired for and/or with access affected
            or restriction on use: affected area, land ownership, current land use, total area of landholding for
            each affected land type, number of land owners/land users, number of PAPs.
      •     Public land (pastureland, game hunting grounds, etc.) that will be permanently acquired for and/or
            with access affected or restriction on use: affected area, total area of all pasture land used by each
            affected household (AH) within and outside the Project area and current land use, type of affected
            pasture (e.g., summer, winter, spring and autumn), status of contract with Municipal enterprises or
            herders, quantity of livestock grazing within the affected land, number of affected land users and the
            number of their family members.
      •     Contracts with government agencies for the use of biological resources of the lands, number of wild
            animals, collected plants, number of users of biological resources.
      •     Trees and long-term crops: quantity and type of affected crop/tree, use of crops/tree (e.g., fruits,
            trees) for commercial sale, household consumption or any other purposes, number of affected
            households and individuals.
      •     Houses and other fixed structures upon land (houses, huts, sheepfolds, sheds, barns, fences, and
            trough pens, etc.): quantity of affected structures, affected area, type of structure, construction
            materials of roof, wall, floor, current use, structure ownership, number of structure users, number of
            physically displaced households . Determine the impact extent (partially affected, fully affected or
            partially affected but the remaining portion of the structure is no longer viable for continued use as its
            original function). All structures should be included in the inventory regardless of whether they are
            permanently inhabited or occupied intermittently by transient populations.
      •     Public or community structures (roads, bridges, irrigation water system, etc.): dimensions of affected
            structures, owners of affected structures, extent of impacts on access of local communities, etc.




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



    •    Cultural assets (graves, burial sites, etc.): quantity of affected graves, grave ownership, names and
         cultural or spiritual significance of burial sites and other cultural assets to local communities,
         implications for local customs, practices, and identity.
    •    Sources of income and livelihood: main source of household income/livelihood, average income,
         quantity of affected livestock, etc.
(ii) For AHs who are herders that have income/livelihood affected, the following information to-be
     collected:
    •    Number of years working as a herder;
    •    Types of livestock managed (sheep, goats, cattle, yaks, etc.)
    •    Number of livestock under their care
    •    Seasonal patterns (e.g., year-round, seasonal herding)
    •    Type of pastures used (summer, spring, winter)
    •    Monthly/seasonal income from herder activities
    •    Whether herder activity is their primary source of income
    •    Other income-generating activities (if any)
•    Estimated income loss due to loss of pasture or job displacement
(iii) Vulnerable PAPs need to be enumerated which include the followings. Total number of people
      living in each AH should be listed.
    •    Low-income households
    •    Households headed by female with dependents;
    •    Households headed by elderly person with no means of support;
    •    Households having people with disabilities; and
    •    Other vulnerable households (if any)
     • The set of criteria that will be discussed and agreed upon with the Community Representative
     Committees (CRCs).
(iv) Other land users. A hunting farm is an organization that has territory secured on a long-term
     lease basis, where sport and foreign hunting is conducted and a range of hunting and
     biotechnical measures are carried out aimed at protecting and reproducing the population of
     game animals and maintaining their numbers at an optimal level or not exceeding the
     ecological capacity of the land).
    •    Hunting grounds are land and forest areas, mountain ranges, water areas and swamps that serve or
         can serve as habitat for wild animals, regardless of the ownership of these territories.
    •    Mapping materials are cartographic materials containing detailed characteristics of forests and
         hunting grounds, varying in scale, topographic and special load depending on their intended purpose.

5.2 Socio-economic Survey (SES)
The SES will be carried out to establish baseline socio-economic status and living standards which
will become the basis for measuring the changes in the living standards during the Project
implementation and end of the Project implementation. The survey shall cover all impacted PAPs in
particular all pastures users and the survey shall also collect gender-disaggregated data to address
gender issues in resettlement. The SES involves the application of quantitative methods (e.g.,
household socio-economic questionnaires) and qualitative methods (community, and resource
mapping, FGDs, and KIIs). Depending on the results of the IOL, the household survey size can be re-




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



determined in consultation with the PMO and World Bank before the SES is conducted. However, it
is required the survey cover at minimum :
    •    100% of winter pasture users and 50% of other pasture users;
    •    100% of households with loss of structures; and
    •    100% of vulnerable AHs.
Detailed tasks of the SES include:
    •    Design survey instruments for review and approval by K1-PMO and WB.
    •    Organize trainings for survey team.
    •    Sampling and selection of households: From the lists of affected households generated from the IOL
         to select households to be surveyed. Ensure representation across locations and impact categories.
    •    Pilot testing and refinement of the survey instruments and sampling protocols.
    •    Survey implementation: Conduct of household survey: carry out face-to-face interviews using
         structured questionnaires; ensure informed consent and privacy of respondents and collect GPS
         coordinates and take photographs (with permission) where necessary to validate locations and
         conditions; conduct KIIs and FGDs.
    •    Data entering, processing and analysing using Excel, SPSS, or other suitable software.
         The SES shall be carried out to capture details of the following aspects
    •    Household identification: Household ID, name and gender identity of household head,
         address/location details, identification number, contact details;
    •    A profile of household members (full name, gender, age, ethnicity, religion, languages, relationship to
         the household head, marital status, highest educational attainment, main and secondary occupations,
         monthly income of each household member);
    •    Economic activities: average monthly household income by income source and average household
         expenditures, savings and debt status, livestock, pasture use, and farming practices;
    •    Land use, land tenure, and land governance;
    •    Access to and use of natural resources (including foraging, hunting, grazing, etc.) – list of seasonal
         activities, locations, products gathered for self-consumption and sale, member’s time spent in
         foraging and other resource-based activities;
    •    Pasture management, pasture use practices, and challenges in pasture use;
    •    Standard of living: housing type and ownership, ownership of household assets, primary and
         secondary sources of fuel, drinking water, and electricity for cooking and heating, toilet facilities, and
         disposal system;
    •    Availability and accessibility to public infrastructure (schools, markets, public transport, health clinic,
         hospital);
    •    Health: type of health care, provider, type of illness or injury, selected questions on women’s and
         young children’s health;
    •    Social aid and government support;
    •    Perceived benefits and impacts of the Project;
    •    Preferences for compensation, assistance, resettlement, and livelihood restoration, and
    •    Skills, training, and resources required by AHs to restore or improve their livelihoods.




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



5.3 Database Development
The Consultant shall be responsible for designing, developing, and maintaining an effective, secure,
and scalable database management system to support land acquisition, involuntary resettlement,
and livelihood restoration planning and LRRP1 implementation in the future.
    •    Establish a system to store and manage resettlement data, allowing for comparative
         analysis of pre- and post-project socio-economic conditions of affected persons and
         communities.
    •    Capture the nature, type, and magnitude of physical and economic losses of affected
         people, enterprises, and public assets.
    •    Support determination of compensation and resettlement entitlements by linking
         household-level socio-economic data to verified loss data.
    •    Track the progress of activities related to land acquisition and involuntary resettlement.
    •    Monitor progress on compensation disbursement and grievance resolution;
    •    Track the implementation of relocation, skills training and livelihood
         restoration/enhancement;
    •    Monitor the restoration of common property resources; and
    •    Generate reliable and timely information for decision-making to project authorities and
         resettlement specialists.
A dedicated Data Manager from the Consultant’s team will lead the development and ongoing
maintenance of the database system. The database will consolidate findings from the IOL and SES,
including both household-level and community-level data. The structure of the database shall be
finalized in consultation with the Client prior to field data collection, ensuring that it is fit-for-
purpose and adaptable to future phases, including compensation administration and LRRP1
implementation.
The database needs to meet the following requirements:
    •    All data shall be stored in digital format, with a secure, easy-to-use interface for authorized users.
    •    Each affected land parcel and fixed asset shall be geo-referenced using GPS coordinates, enabling
         accurate mapping, spatial analysis, and future verification.
    •    A unique identifier will be assigned to each household, enterprise, and affected asset to enable
         traceability and ensure seamless cross-referencing with SES data, eligibility assessments, and
         compensation records.
    •    The IOL findings must be disaggregated into three categories:
    (i) Affected households’ land and asset inventory,
    (ii) Affected enterprise losses, and
    (iii) Losses of community-level or public assets (e.g., roads, bridges, irrigation infrastructure,
          schools, water sources).
    •    The database must support integration and storage of photographs and geotagged videos of affected
         assets to enable quick, cost-effective retrieval while avoiding duplication.
    •    The database must include functionality for automated data validation to flag inconsistencies and
         minimize entry errors and regular automatic backups to safeguard data and prevent data loss.




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



5.4 Replacement Cost Survey and Calculation of Compensation Rates
Following the results of the IOL for the land acquisition for construction site and associated
facilities, the consultant will carry out a Replacement Cost Survey (RCS) for potentially affected land
and non-land assets in accordance with national regulations and full replacement cost principles of
World Bank policies. The RCS is to establish the basis for calculation of replacement costs for all the
lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project. In relation to this, RCS needs to be
completed to establish compensation rates for the LRRP1 that is prepared under the Project. Based
on the RCS results, calculation of compensation will be carried out based on the Entitlement Matrix
approved as part of LRRF.
(i) Land: Conduct interviews with Representatives from the relevant agencies (e.g., Aiyl Okmotu
    of affected AAs, District level cadastral unit branches of the State Agency of Land Resources,
    Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography), affected and unaffected landowners in the Project area
    to collect information on:
    •    Recent market transactions and informal sales of land use rights.
    •    Willingness-to-sell prices of both affected and unaffected households.
    •    Associated costs (e.g., transaction cost, taxes, administrative charges, registration or title fees,
         reasonable moving expenses, and any similar costs imposed on affected persons).
    •    The replacement cost of affected land is equivalent to current market price, transaction costs, taxes,
         and other administrative costs.
(ii) Crops and Trees: Interview affected households, farmers, and local agricultural officers to
     assess:
    •    For crops: The market prices for different types of perennial and annual crops over the past three
         years, crop yield per hectare.
    •    For fruit or productive trees: cost of seedlings, the number of years required for seedlings to reach
         maturity by species, average yield/value of mature trees per year and market prices of output (fruits,
         nuts, etc.) or prices at which tree owners are willing to sell their produce.
    •    For timber trees: timber volume, and quality of each type of affected trees (species, diameter, height,
         age, and condition; current market price per cubic meter of timber.
(iii) Structures: Interview representatives of District Departments of Urban Planning and
      Architecture of the State Agency for Architecture, Construction, and Housing and Communal
      Services under the Cabinet of Ministers of the Kyrgyz Republic), affected households, local
      builders, and construction firms to determine:
    •    Types of construction materials usually used in the locality for each type of affected structures;
    •    Sources of construction materials used;
    •    Unit costs of said materials, including the costs of transporting the same to the locality; and
    •    Cost of labour for constructing each type of affected structures;
    •    Expenses related to obtaining building permits and registrations, if applicable.
     •  Replacement cost for affected structures is equivalent to the current market price for materials, labor,
     and other expenses related to obtaining building permits and registrations, if applicable.
(iv) Other cost and allowance: Interview local residents to determine
    •    Cost of excavation, relocation, reburial and other related costs
    •    Transportation costs for movable assets, including salvaged materials from original structures
(v) Price Comparison and Validation:




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



    •    Compare estimated replacement costs with the unit rates approved by the State Agency for
         Architecture, Construction, and Housing and Communal Services or other relevant bodies, if available.
    •    Consult with district- and AA-level authorities to verify and validate findings.
(vi) Cost Estimation and Reporting:
    •    Propose unit rates for compensation of affected assets (land, structures, perennial and annual crops)
         based on replacement cost principles and without depreciation in consultation with PMO and World
         Bank;
    •    Calculate the cost of compensation, assistance, and resettlement.

5.5 Public Consultations
     •   The consultant is required to conduct the following activities:
    •    Carrying out a series of public consultation meetings including one consultative meeting with local
         authorities and relevant agencies at district and AA levels and one meeting with potentially affected
         households in each AA before the commencement of the IOL, SES, and RCS.
    •    The Project information to be shared and consulted with potentially affected people and communities
         includes, but not limited to:

    •    Project description and expected benefits of the Project;
    •    Potential land acquisition and resettlement impacts due to the construction site and
         associated facilities;
    •    Feasible measures to minimize and mitigate the land acquisition and resettlement impacts;
    •    Proposed eligibility and entitlements for PAPs;
    •    Availability of replacement land;
    •    Restoration of loss of access to pasture land;
    •    Needs of PAPs in livelihood restoration and relocation preference;
    •    Schedules for the IOL, SES, and RCS;
    •    Mechanisms for continuing meaningful consultation with and participation of PAPs,
         community, and other stakeholders in land acquisition and resettlement planning,
         implementation, and monitoring; and grievance redress mechanism.
    •    Consider as of inception the establishment of Community Resettlement Committees (CRC) at the level
         of each affected AA that will act throughout the land acquisition and resettlement planning process as
         negotiation instances between the Project and the Consultant on the one hand, and the community
         on the other. Establishment and composition of the CRCs will be discussed with community leadership
         and local authorities. CRCs should be inclusive of all pertinent layers of the affected population,
         including youth, women and vulnerable groups. Establishing CRCs as the main negotiation and
         interaction avenue should not pre-empt other consultation avenues, including focus groups and
         general community meetings.
    •    Organizing public consultation meetings with PAPs and local authorities after completion of the IOL,
         SES, and RCS to present survey results, announced the cut-off date for eligibility for compensation,
         assistance, and resettlement, and discussed the proposed entitlements with PAPs and communities.
    •    Organizing public consultation meetings with PAPs and local authorities on the provisions of the draft
         LRRP1 before submission to World Bank for review and approval.
    •    Conducting in-depth interviews with key-informants (e.g., leaders of AA, village heads, Municipal
         Enterprises, District Agriculture Management, Department of Pastures and Breeding Livestock,
         Women’s Union) to obtain their insights about the project’s impacts on local residents and LRP (if any).




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



    •    Organizing FGDs with specific groups of PAPs (e.g., vulnerable households, affected non-timber forest
         product collectors, affected women) to understand their unique concerns, vulnerabilities, and
         recommendations.
These consultation activities should be held at a suitable time and place for women, and should also
take into account the needs of persons with disabilities (if any), as well as any barriers faced by
socially vulnerable groups, should also be considered when organizing such events. Whenever
possible, meetings should be held in neutral, accessible public spaces or within women-led civil
society organizations, where available.
All presentations must be delivered in the Kyrgyz language, and Project Information Booklets should
be distributed to all participants. All the concerns, suggestions, and recommendations raised by
meeting participants must be recorded and documented. This includes compiling attendance sheets
and photographic evidence of the consultations.
5.6 Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM)
The grievance redress mechanism (GRM) shall be developed in accordance with the Project’s
Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP), the LRRF, and the WB’s ESS10. In particular, the GRM will be
developed based on current ongoing GRM practices that have been applied locally as per national
laws and regulations and their design takes into account the views of affected communities
expressed during the LRRP1 preparation. Particular attention will be given to ensuring the GRM is
accessible, inclusive, and responsive, with specific provisions to facilitate access for disadvantaged
and vulnerable individuals or groups.
5.7 Special Considerations for the Needs of Women
All transactions related to physical or economic displacement require particular attention to gender.
For example:
    •    Intra-household analysis may be needed where women’s and men’s livelihoods are affected
         differently.
    •    Women’s and men’s preferences in terms of compensation mechanisms, such as replacement land or
         alternative access to natural resources rather than in cash, should be explored
    •    Documentation of ownership or occupancy and compensation payments should be issued in the name
         of both spouses or single female heads of households
    •    Propose land acquisition, resettlement, and livelihood restoration measures, such as skills training, job
         opportunities etc., should be equally available to women and adapted to their needs
    •    The consultation process should ensure that women’s perspectives are obtained, and their interests
         factored in.

6. Specific Tasks for the preparation of the Due Diligence Review on the
   land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement activities
   implemented for the early works and associated facilities
A Due Diligence Report (DDR) will be prepared for early works and associated facilities. The
objectives of the Due Diligence Review are the following:
    •    Evaluate if all involuntary resettlement activities associated with the early works and associated
         Facilities were carried out in full compliance with regulations of Kyrgyz Republic.
    •    Confirm if the compensation payment/provision of support/resettlement done by local government
         (including its resettlement outcome) meets the objectives of ESS5.
    •    Check if there are any resettlement related issues that remain pending at the time of the due
         diligence.




                                                                                                                     Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework



    •    Assess potential reputational risks for the GoKR and the World Bank regarding resettlement-related
         activities for this Project.
The consultant will undertake the following key tasks:
    •    Review documents related to land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement activities
         undertaken for early works and the associated facilities including, among others, registered lands in
         the Zembalance.
    •    Conduct site visits in affected villages and public consultations with affected people, relevant
         agencies to collect quantitative and qualitative information for assessing the performance and
         effectiveness (including how the land was occupied or used) of the land acquisition, compensation,
         assistance, and resettlement in line with the WB’s ESS5 requirements, and satisfaction of the affected
         people with the resettlement process.
    •    Assess the compliance of compensation, assistance, and resettlement implemented for the early
         works and associated facilities with national legislation and objectives and requirements of the ESS5.
    •    Identify discrepancies between the implemented compensation, assistance, and resettlement and
         requirements of national laws and regulations as well as the ESS5.
    •    Discuss the identified gaps or non-compliance issues with the K1-PMO and relevant agencies.
    •    Provide recommendations for corrective actions to address identified gaps or non-compliance issues,
         including preparation of a Corrective Action Plan with timelines, responsibilities, and budget.

7. Deliverables and Timeframe
The consultant shall submit the following reports:
    •    Inception Report: This report will present the methodology, resources, tools, and detailed schedule
         for delivering the assignment’s objectives and scope of work. It will include a detailed outline of the
         LRRP1 structure, in accordance with the Project's LRRF and the World Bank’s ESS 5 and other
         international standards. Additionally, it also includes the update of the screening report will be also
         included in the Inception Report. The Inception Report shall be submitted to the K1-PMO, the World
         Bank and other Lenders for approval within one (1) week of contract signing.
    •    Draft LRRP1: This report will cover the full scope of work outlined in the TOR and will be prepared
         following comprehensive stakeholder engagement and consultation. The draft LRRP1 will be
         submitted to K1-PMO, the World Bank and other Lenders for review within nine (9) weeks of contract
         signing.
    •    Final LRRP1: This report will incorporate feedback from the Client, stakeholders, the World Bank,
         and other Lenders ensuring all review comments are addressed and will be submitted within eleven
         (11) weeks of contract signing.
    •    Final database in agreed format (e.g., Excel with GIS shape files or web-based format), photo and

         consultation meetings, FGDs, and KIIs.
    •    Due Diligence Review on the land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement activities
         implemented for the early works and associated facilities of the Project, including the preparation of a
         Corrective Action Plan with timelines, responsibilities, and budget.
•    All deliverables must be submitted in English and Kyrgyz in both editable (Word, Excel, etc.) and PDF
     formats.
