            ANNEX 4.2: Draft TOR for LRRP for RESERVOIR-IMPOUNDED AREA AND WATER
                                        PROTECTION ZONE

1.       Introduction and Background
The Government of the Kyrgyz Republic has prioritized the development of its hydropower
potential as a central pillar of national energy security and sustainable economic growth. Given the
country’s mountainous terrain and rich water resources, particularly from the Naryn River basin,
the hydropower sector plays a critical role in domestic energy supply and regional energy
cooperation.
As part of this national strategy, the Government, through the Ministry of Energy is seeking the
financing for development of the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Plant (K-1 HPP)—a major infrastructure
project that aligns with the objectives set out in the Sustainable Development Strategy (2018–2040)
and the National Development Program to 2026. Once operational, K-1 HPP is expected to be the
largest hydropower project in the Kyrgyz Republic and the broader Central Asia region, with an
installed capacity of approximately 1,880 MW and annual generation of about 5,961 GWh—
equivalent to nearly 50% of the country’s current installed capacity. K-1 HPP is expected to improve
the energy and food security of the Kyrgyz Republic while enhancing the country’s energy export
revenue through the distribution of surplus power to other Central Asian countries, including
Uzbekistan, Tajikistan and Pakistan. The large reservoir of K-1 HPP on the Naryn River is expected to
improve the operation of the Toktogul HPP reservoir, which can provide a much-needed balance to
the water management regime in the Naryn–Syr Darya Basin. The proposed Project is a crucial step
in fulfilling the government’s vision for a green and affordable energy future.
The proposed site for the K-1 HPP is located in the middle reaches of the Naryn River, about 14.5
km upstream of the existing Kambarata-2 HPP dam, in the Toktogul and Toguz-Toro Districts of
Jalalabad Region.




                                                                                                       Figure
1-1 shows the K-1 HPP dam site location and the reservoir.




                                                                                                       Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework




Figure 1-1: Kambarata-1 HPP dam site location and the reservoir

The proposed Project consists of the following main elements:
     •    A roller-compacted concrete (RCC) gravity dam of 10 m wide at the crest with a maximum height
          above the riverbed of 260.8 m.
     •    A reservoir area of 61.7 km2 at a full supply level (FSL) of 1,198 msl. The inundated area extends
          approximately 68 km upstream from the dam wall.
     •    An overground powerhouse including Francis-type turbines with a total electricity generating capacity
          of 1,880 MW.
     •    The construction of temporary and permanent access roads, transport tunnel, and bridge structures
          within the dam site.
     •    The construction of water pipelines and tunnels.
     •    Quarry sites to source raw materials for the dam.
     •    A temporary concrete batching plant, materials storage, waste disposal, and quarries, workshops .
     •    Permanent and temporary accommodation facilities for dam and hydropower operations and
          maintenance personnel.
     •    Early works, including the mobilization of early works contractor, access roads to left bank, bridge to
          powerhouse, bridge to right bank, access roads to right bank, access road to river diversion inlet and
          outlet structures, camp and workshop for early works contract, 2 no. diversion tunnels including inlets
          and outlets, excavation of dam left and right abutments down to river level, excavation of power
          intake structures down to 1125 masl, excavation of powerhouse and substation area to 966.4 masl.
     •    Associated facilities.
As part of the Project preparation, the Ministry of Energy (MoE), through its Project Management
Office (PMO), has engaged SMEC to undertake a comprehensive Environmental and Social Impact
Assessment (ESIA). This assessment seeks to comply with the international Environmental and
Social guidelines and standards from World Bank (WB), Asian Development Bank (ADB), Asian
Infrastructure Development Bank (AIIB), European Investment Bank Environmental and Social


                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

Sustainability Framework, European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), and Islamic
Development Bank and relevant national legislation. In line with the requirements of the
international standards regarding Land Acquisition, Restrictions on Land Use, and Involuntary
Resettlement – a Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework (LRRF) has also been
developed for submission to the World Bank for review and approval. Two Livelihood Restoration
and Resettlement Plans (LRRPs) will be prepared under this framework:
    •    LRRP1 – covering land acquisition for construction site and associated facilities;
    •    LRRP2 – to address impacts related to the reservoir impoundment area and the water protection zone
         (WPZ).
These Terms of Reference (TOR) has been developed for the LRRP2 preparation.

2. Preliminary Identification of Land Acquisition and Resettlement Impacts
   due to Reservoir Area and Water Protection Zone
The following sections present a summary of the findings from the ESIA conducted by SMEC in
2025, specifically focusing on potential impacts related to land acquisition and resettlement within
the reservoir area and Water Protection Zone (WPZ). These findings are based on (i) consultations
held with Municipal Enterprises of the affected Aiyl Aimaks in February 2025, (ii) the most recent
data provided by the Pasture Management Consultants in May 2025, and (iii) GIS mapping and
household surveys carried out on 337 households in November 2024.
2.1 Potential Impacts due to Reservoir Area
Permanent Impacts on Land
Based on the draft K1 ESIA6,170 hectares (equivalent to 61.7 km2) of land will be required at a
water level of 1,198 meters. Most of the inundated area (5,851.42 ha, 94.84%) is located in
Toktogul district, covering lands from the following AAs: E. Imanaliev, Sary-Kamysh, and Toluk. The
remaining 5.16% of the affected land falls within Atai and Kargalyk AAs of Toguz-Toro district and
Minkush AA of Jumgal district. The consultant should verify, confirm and update the scope of
impacts on land as part of this assignment.
Early consultations carried out in Toluk and Sary-Kamysh Aas during the preparation of the draft K1
ESIA reported that residents do not hold legal documents for land within the inundation zone, as a
significant part of the area has belonged to Electric Power Plant OSJC since 2013. However, in
Nichke-Sai and Chorgochu villages, two households were reported to possibly possess such
documents, including Cholponkulov Murat, who was allocated land by a 1998 local council decision.
Two State Acts confirming land rights in the Uch-Terek area were also presented, though they
require further legal review. The consultant should verify, confirm and update this and other
relevant land ownership and land use documentation in the project area.
Also as part of the draft K1 ESIA, it has been reported that part of the land is legally owned by the
Electric Power Plants OSJC, but it continues to be used in practice as pasture by residents of the
Sary-Kamysh, Toluk, Imanaliev, and Atai AAs. The consultant should verify, confirm and update this
information about the current formal and informal land use of the land included into this
assignment.
Loss of Access to Pastureland
The draft K1 ESIA has indicated that 83.42 km of horse and foot trails will be inundated by the
reservoir. In addition, eleven bridges, including two bridges used to cross the Toluk River and
Temirken River will be submerged under water. Therefore, in addition to the direct loss of
pastureland from reservoir submergence, villagers in Toluk AA may lose access to remaining grazing
areas once the reservoir is filled. The assessment of Pasture Management Consultants conducted in


                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

consultation with local authorities indicate that in addition to pastures that will be submerged,
1,394 hectares of winter pasture may become inaccessible due to the loss of bridges and horse
paths in Toluk. The number of affected pasture users due to loss of access has not yet known. The
consultant should verify, confirm and update the scope of impacts on loss of access to pastureland
as part of this assignment.
Impacts on Structures
Also following the draft K1 ESIA, 41 structures owned by 41 households (245 persons) will be
potentially affected. Data from the household survey conducted in October and November 2024
indicated that among the 337 surveyed households, 13 households with 91 persons claimed that
their livestock pens, primarily made of wood, are located within the reservoir area of the Project.
The ESIA findings indicate that three households reside in the affected pasture areas in E. Imanaliev
AA. These households may be physically displaced as a result of land acquisition for the reservoir
area. In addition to the previously mentioned structure, three water mills will be affected and the
inundation zone also covers a traditional salt extraction site used for livestock, which will be
submerged.
The number of potentially affected structures, the number of affected households and persons,
purpose of use, severity of impacts (partial loss or full loss) will be validated during RP preparation.
The consultant should verify, confirm and update the scope of impacts on structures as part of this
assignment.
Impacts on Crops and Trees
The draft K1 ESIA reports that, among the 337 surveyed households, 9 households (52 persons)
reported that they have crops and trees in the reservoir area (i.e. orchards and vegetables). The
consultant should verify, confirm and update the scope of impacts on crops and trees as part of this
assignment.
Impacts on Public Infrastructures
The draft K1 ESIA findings indicate that no school, healthcare facilities, irrigation, and water supply
system will be impacted by the Project. The consultant should verify, confirm and update the scope
of impacts on public infrastructure as part of this assignment.
Impacts on Cultural Assets and Graves
The draft K1 ESIA informs that a total of 14 cultural heritage sites, including burial mounds, rock art
complexes, traditional structures, and sacred landscapes are located in the reservoir area, therefore
directly impacted. There are also a number of graves The consultant should verify, confirm and
update the scope of impacts on cultural assets and graves as part of this assignment.
Impacts on Livelihood
The draft K1 ESIA states that the reservoir’s inundation is expected to cause significant economic
displacement for communities in the four affected AAs, primarily impacting livestock herding and
beekeeping. Livestock production—responsible for up to 95% of household income—will suffer
from the submergence of 3,538 hectares of pastureland. The K1 ESIA also refers to additional
potential impacts on honey production, forest users and hunters. The consultant should verify,
confirm and update the scope of impacts on livelihoods as part of this assignment.


2.2 Potential Impacts due to Water Protection Zone
Once the reservoir is inundated and in use, there will also be further restriction on land use due to
the water protection zones. The water protection zone (WPZ) for the construction of the reservoir


                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

for the K-1 HPP is set at 500 meters, in accordance with the Regulation "On Water Protection Zones
and Strips of Water Bodies in the Kyrgyz Republic" (July 7, 1995, No. 271). According to draft K1
ESIA, approximately 9,599 hectares (equivalent to 95.99 km2) of land will be affected by the WPZ.
The area is predominantly public land (including water bodies, shrubs land), covering approximately
4,916.08 hectares (51.21%), followed by pasture land at 4,683.07 hectares (48.79%). There is no
agriculture land in the WPZ. The GIS mapping indicated that it is estimated that 15 structures may
be affected.
Always following the initial findings of the draft K1 ESIA, it is estimated that 1,024 pasture users —
or around 6,211 individuals—will be affected by both the reservoir and the WPZ. This estimate was
developed in consultation with Municipal Enterprises, primarily considering pasture users in the
reservoir area. It is based on the assumption that individuals affected by the reservoir's
submergence and pasture use restrictions due to the establishment of the WPZ will overlap, given
local land use practices. The consultant should verify, confirm and update the scope of impacts due
to the Water Protection Zone, in case this case is confirmed.

3. Objectives of Consultancy Services
The task required is to prepare a Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Plan for the reservoir-
impounded area and WPZ of the K-1 HPP Project (LRRP2). The LRRP2 preparation must be compliant
with the Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework (LRRF) of the Project, international
social standards such as Environmental and Social Framework from the World Bank (WB), the
Environmental and Social Framework of the Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB), the
European Investment Bank (EIB)’s Environmental and Social Sustainability Framework, the European
Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD)’s Environmental and Social Performance
Requirements and the Kyrgyz Republic’s relevant laws and regulations. The document must comply
with the requirements of the WB’s ESS5.

4. Scope of Works
The Consultant’s tasks shall include, but not be limited to, the following:
    •    Prepare an inception report detailing the methodology used to prepare the LRRP2. This inception
         report will be submitted to K1-PMO and the WB for approval.
    •    Update the social screening conducted in 2025 the by the K1 ESIA consultant (SMEC), covering,
         among others, the rapid preliminary assessment to collect information on proposed land location,
         area, ownership details, current land use, tenure status of present land use and unit of government
         having jurisdiction on land.
    •    Carry out a census (including establishing a cut-off date) and an inventory of loss (IOL) to identify the
         persons who will be affected by the Project, to establish an inventory of land and assets to be
         affected, to determine who will be eligible for compensation and assistance, and to discourage
         ineligible persons, such as opportunistic settlers, from claiming benefits. The exercise will be
         conducted using a structured questionnaire. The consultant will develop a database of physical
         quantities of impacts and lay down the basis for developing an entitlement policy and compensation
         package.
    •    Disseminate the cut-off date that will be notified by MoE to all Project Affected People (PAPs)
         throughout the resettlement planning in the project area in a clear and transparent manner. The cut-
         off date will also be documented in the LRRP.
    •    Conduct a socio-economic survey (SES) to establish baseline data for use in the description of PAPs,
         provide a basis for the design of, and budgeting for, the resettlement program, and inform baseline
         for monitoring and evaluation of land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement of the
         Project.
    •    Deliver a GIS-compatible database of affected assets and affected people capturing information
         gathered in SES and IOL, the structure of which will be agreed with the K1 PMO and the Government
         of Kyrgyz Republic (GoKR) prior to survey inception, and which will be designed upfront to evolve and


                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

         be used in further steps (LRRP2 implementation) as the main database for compensation
         administration (preparation of compensation agreements) and livelihood restoration monitoring.
    •    Conduct a Replacement Costs Survey (RCS). The RCS will need to be carried out to establish the basis
         for calculation of replacement costs for all the lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project.
         In relation to this, RCS needs to be completed to establish compensation rates for the LRRP2. The
         consultant will calculate the cost of compensation, assistance, and resettlement based on the RCS
         results and the Entitlement Matrix approved as part of LRRF.
    •    Conduct consultations with PAPs, local authorities, Non-government Organizations (NGOs) and
         relevant stakeholder through public consultation meetings, focus group discussions (FGDs), key-
         informant interviews (KIIs), and in-depth face-to-face interviews in Kyrgyz or Russian language to
         ascertain their opinions, concerns about various aspects of land acquisition, in particular entitlements
         on compensation, assistance, and resettlement, replacement pasture, restoration of loss of access to
         pastureland and livelihood restoration. Take the opinions and concerns into account and ensure they
         are addressed and incorporated into the LRRP2.
    •    Consultations with women and vulnerable groups, in particular, will be carried out to understand their
         specific concerns and views. Based on the outcome of these consultations, if required, suitable
         mitigation measures will be incorporated into the Project and LRRP2.
    •    Prepare a LRRP2 for the reservoir – impounded area and WPZ based on the outcome of the IOL, SES,
         RCS, ESIA and the LRRF. The LRRP2 will also include entitlements for different types of impacts, socio
         economic characteristics of the affected persons, institutional mechanisms, implementation schedules,
         budgets, grievance redress mechanism, coordination of implementation in conjunction with civil works
         procurement and construction schedules and monitoring mechanisms. The LRRP2 will comply with the
         principles outlined in the LRRF and the WB’s ESS5. The outline of the LRRP2 is attached in Appendix
         1.
    •    Prepare a Livelihood Restoration Program. The LRP prepared under this LRRF will be updated
         following new consultations with communities and PAPs.

5. Specific Tasks
5.1 Census and Inventory of Losses
The census and IOL shall be carried out for 100% of the affected households using a structured
questionnaire to record the details of the affected persons. The exercise will help to: (i) obtain a full
inventory of affected assets that will support the determination of compensation for each and
every of these assets; (ii) prevent further influx of persons within the identified project area; (iii)
assess the magnitude of impact to private assets and livelihoods; and (iv) Assess the extent of
physical and/or economic displacement. The census and the IOL will be based on the preliminary
design included in the feasibility study. It is important to cover all people adversely affected by the
reservoir area and WPZ, regardless of their legal status – landowners, land users, holders of land
rights, tenants, illegal squatter – or whether they are actually living on the affected site at the time
of the census and IOL. In other words, private landowners and holders of rights to land as well as
any person currently occupying public or private land for shelter, business purposes, or other
sources of livelihood should be included in the census and IOL.
Consultant is asked to identify the persons who will be affected by the project, and establish an
inventory of land and assets to be affected following the steps below:
    (i) Develop a structured questionnaire for review and approval by K1-PMO and World Bank.
    (ii) Approach the Municipal Enterprises and those in charge of land management who holds the land
         records to collect (or purchase) of cadastral maps/land use maps on the project villages and Ayil
         Aimaks (AAs).
    (iii) Overlay the map of the reservoir area and WPZ on the land use maps of the relevant AAs. This
          method will provide basic information such as types of affected lands; amounts of affected lands;
          number of the plots, etc. The consultant will review of cadastral records together with the Municipal
          Enterprises and land management officers and village and AA leaders.




                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

    (iv) Lay-out the reservoir area and WPZ on the ground with support of a design engineer, representatives
         from Municipal Enterprises, village leaders/AA leaders and GPS, the consultant will identify the
         location of the project area in the field and identify the impacts within the reservoir area and WPZ;
    (v) Together with village leaders and Municipal Enterprises of affected AAs to identify the affected
        households and conduct interviews with household heads or their spouses using the questionnaire to
        determine their scope of land acquisition impacts.
    (vi) Take photos of affected households (the heads of household - husband and wife - or with many
         household members as possible) with their household ID in front of their affected house/land with
         embedded coordinates (using GPS-enabled cameras or mobile apps) , previous written permission
         provided.
    (vii) Separate data from the reservoir and the WPZ.
    (viii)        Analyse the data on the land acquisition impacts for both the reservoir and the WPZ.
     •    All the IOL information must be geo-referenced.
The following data and information need to be collected during the IOL, but not limited to:
    (i)       Affected assets that need to be enumerated for the impounded area and the WPZ:
    •     Private land (agricultural land, etc.) that will be permanently acquired for and/or with access affected
          or restriction on use: affected area, land ownership, current land use, total area of landholding for
          each affected land type, number of land owners/land users, number of Project Affected Persons
          (PAPs).
    •     Public land (pastureland, etc.) that will be permanently acquired for and/or with access affected or
          restriction on use: affected area, total area of all pasture land used by each PAP within and outside
          the project area and current land use, type of affected pasture (e.g., summer, winter, spring and
          autumn), status of contract with Municipal enterprises or herders, quantity of livestock grazing within
          the affected land, number of affected land users and the number of their family members.
    •     Trees and long-term crops: quantity and type of affected crop/tree, use of crops/tree (e.g., fruits,
          trees) for sale or for household consumption or any other purposes, number of affected households
          and individuals.
    •     Houses and other fixed structures upon land (houses, huts, sheepfolds, sheds, barns, fences, and
          trough pens, beehives etc.): quantity of affected structures, affected area, type of structure,
          construction materials of roof, wall, floor, current use, structure ownership, number of structure
          users, number of physically displaced households. Determine the impact extent (partially affected,
          fully affected or partially affected but the remaining portion of the structure is no longer viable for
          continued use as its original function). All structures should be included in the inventory regardless of
          whether they are permanently inhabited or occupied intermittently by transient populations.
    •     Public or community structures (roads, bridges, irrigation water system, etc.): dimensions of affected
          structures, owners of affected structures, extent of impacts on access of local communities, etc.
    •     Cultural assets (graves, burial sites, etc.): quantity of affected graves, grave ownership, names and
          cultural or spiritual significance of burial sites and other cultural assets to local communities,
          implications for local customs, practices, and identity.
    •     Sources of income and livelihood: main source of household income/livelihood, average income,
          quantity of affected livestock, etc.
(ii) For AHs who are herders that have income/livelihood affected, the following information to-be
     collected:
    •     Number of years working as a herder;
    •     Types of livestock managed (sheep, goats, cattle, yaks, etc.)
    •     Number of livestock under their care
    •     Seasonal patterns (e.g., year-round, seasonal herding)
    •     Type of pastures used (summer, spring, winter)
    •     Monthly/seasonal income from herder acitivities



                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

    •    Whether herder activity is their primary source of income
    •    Other income-generating activities (if any)
    •    Estimated income loss due to loss of pasture or job displacement
(iii) Vulnerable PAPs need to be enumerated which include the followings. Total number of people
      living in each AH should be listed.
    •    Low-income households
    •    Households headed by female with dependents;
    •    Households headed by elderly person with no means of support;
    •    Households having people with disabilities; and
    •    Other vulnerable households (if any)
     • The set of criteria that will be discussed and agreed upon with the Community Representative
     Committees (CRCs)



5.2 Socio-economic Survey
The SES will be carried out to establish baseline socio-economic status and living standards which
will become the basis for measuring the changes in the living standards during the Project
implementation and end of the Project implementation. The survey shall cover all impacted PAPs in
particular all pastures users and the survey shall also collect gender-disaggregated data to address
gender issues in resettlement. The SES involves the application of quantitative methods (e.g.,
household socio-economic questionnaires) and qualitative methods (community, and resource
mapping, FGDs, and KIIs). Depending on the results of the IOL, the household survey size and the
number of FGDs, KIIs, and targeted stakeholders can be re-determined in consultation with the
PMO and World Bank before the SES is conducted. However, it is required the survey cover at
minimum
    •    100% of winter pasture users and 50% of other pasture users;
    •    100% of households with loss of structures; and
    •    100% of vulnerable AHs.
Detailed tasks of the SES include:
    •    Develop the survey instrument for review and approval by K1-PMO and World Bank.
    •    Sampling and selection of households: From the lists of affected households generated from the IOL
         to select households to be surveyed. Ensure representation across locations and impact categories.
    •    Organize trainings for survey team.
    •    Pilot testing and refinement of the survey instrument and sampling protocols
    •    Survey implementation: Conduct of household survey: carry out face-to-face interviews using
         structured questionnaires; ensure informed consent and privacy of respondents and collect GPS
         coordinates and take photographs (with permission) where necessary to validate locations and
         conditions; Conduct KIIs, and FGDs.
    •    Data entering, processing and analysing using Excel, SPSS, or other suitable software.
The SES shall be carried out to capture details of the following aspects
    •    Household identification: Household ID, name and gender identity of household head,
         address/location details, identification number, contact details;
    •    A profile of household members (full name, gender, age, ethnicity, religion, languages, relationship to
         the household head, marital status, highest educational attainment, main and secondary occupations,
         monthly income of each household member);




                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

    •    Economic activities: average monthly household income by income source and average household
         expenditures, savings and debt status, livestock, pasture use, and farming practices;
    •    Land use, land tenure, and land governance;
    •    Access to and use of natural resources (including foraging, hunting, grazing, etc.) – list of seasonal
         activities, locations, products gathered for self-consumption and sale, member’s time spent in
         foraging and other resource-based activities;
    •    Pasture management, pasture use practices, and challenges in pasture use;
    •    Standard of living: housing type and ownership, ownership of household assets, primary and
         secondary sources of fuel, drinking water, and electricity for cooking and heating, toilet facilities, and
         disposal system;
    •    Availability and accessibility to public infrastructure (schools, markets, public transport, health clinic,
         hospital);
    •    Health: type of health care, provider, type of illness or injury, selected questions on women’s and
         young children’s health;
    •    Social aid and government support;
    •    Perceived benefits and impacts of the Project;
    •    Preferences for compensation, assistance, resettlement, and livelihood restoration, and
    •    Skills, training, and resources required by AHs to restore or improve their livelihoods.

5.3 Database Development
The Consultant shall be responsible for designing, developing, and maintaining an effective, secure,
and scalable database management system to support land acquisition, involuntary resettlement,
and livelihood restoration planning and LRRP2 implementation in the future.
    (i) Establish a system to store and manage resettlement data, allowing for comparative
        analysis of pre- and post-project socio-economic conditions of affected persons and
        communities.
    (ii) Capture the nature, type, and magnitude of physical and economic losses of affected
         people, enterprises, and public assets.
    (iii) Support determination of compensation and resettlement entitlements by linking
          household-level socio-economic data to verified loss data.
    (iv) Track the progress of activities related to land acquisition and involuntary resettlement.
    (v) Monitor progress on compensation disbursement and grievance resolution;
    (vi) Track the implementation of relocation, skills training and livelihood
         restoration/enhancement;
    (vii)         Monitor the restoration of common property resources; and
    (viii)      Generate reliable and timely information for decision-making to project authorities
         and resettlement specialists.
A dedicated Data Manager from the Consultant’s team will lead the development and ongoing
maintenance of the database system. The database will consolidate findings from the IOL and SES,
including both household-level and community-level data. The structure of the database shall be
finalized in consultation with the Client prior to field data collection, ensuring that it is fit-for-
purpose and adaptable to future phases, including compensation administration and LRRP2
implementation.
The database needs to meet the following requirements:
    •    All data shall be stored in digital format, with a secure, easy-to-use interface for authorized users.



                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

    •    Each affected land parcel and fixed asset shall be geo-referenced using GPS coordinates, enabling
         accurate mapping, spatial analysis, and future verification.
    •    A unique identifier will be assigned to each household, enterprise, and affected asset to enable
         traceability and ensure seamless cross-referencing with SES data, eligibility assessments, and
         compensation records.
•    The IOL findings must be disaggregated into three categories:
    (i) Affected households’ land and asset inventory,
    (ii) Affected enterprise losses, and
    (iii) Losses of community-level or public assets (e.g., roads, bridges, irrigation infrastructure,
          schools, water sources).
•    The database must support integration and storage of photographs and geotagged videos of affected
     assets to enable quick, cost-effective retrieval while avoiding duplication.
•    The database must include functionality for automated data validation to flag inconsistencies and
     minimize entry errors and regular automatic backups to safeguard data and prevent data loss.

5.4 Replacement Cost Survey and Calculation of Compensation Rates
Following the results of the Inventory of Losses for the land acquisition for reservoir area and WPZ,
the Consultant will carry out a Replacement Cost Survey (RCS) for potentially affected land and non-
land assets in accordance with national regulations and full replacement cost principles of World
Bank policies. The RCS is to establish the basis for calculation of replacement costs for all the
lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project. In relation to this, RCS needs to be completed
to establish compensation rates for the LRRP2 that is prepared under the Project. Based on the RCS
results, calculation of compensation will be carried out based on the Entitlement Matrix approved
as part of LRRF.
(i) Private Land: Conduct interviews with Representatives from the relevant agencies (e.g., Aiyl
    Okmotu affected AAs, District level cadastral unit branches of the State Agency of Land
    Resources, Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography), affected and unaffected landowners in the
    Project area to collect information on:
    •    Recent market transactions and informal sales of land use rights.
    •    Willingness-to-sell prices of both affected and unaffected households.
    •    Associated costs (e.g., transaction cost, taxes, administrative charges, registration or title fees,
         reasonable moving expenses, and any similar costs imposed on affected persons).
     •  The replacement cost of affected land is equivalent to current market price, transaction costs, taxes,
     and other administrative costs.
(ii) Crops and Trees: Interview affected households, farmers, and local agricultural officers to
     assess:
    •    For crops: The market prices for different types of perennial and annual crops over the past three
         years, crop yield per hectare.
    •    For fruit or productive trees: cost of seedlings, the number of years required for seedlings to reach
         maturity by species, average yield/value of mature trees per year and market prices of output (fruits,
         nuts, etc.) or prices at which tree owners are willing to sell their produce.
    •    For timber trees: timber volume, and quality of each type of affected trees (species, diameter, height,
         age, and condition; current market price per cubic meter of timber.
(iii) Structures: Interview representatives of District Departments of Urban Planning and
      Architecture of the State Agency for Architecture, Construction, and Housing and Communal
      Services under the Cabinet of Ministers of the Kyrgyz Republic), affected households, local
      builders, and construction firms to determine:


                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

    •    Types of construction materials usually used in the locality for each type of affected structures;
    •    Sources of construction materials used;
    •    Unit costs of said materials, including the costs of transporting the same to the locality; and
    •    Cost of labour for constructing each type of affected structures;
    •    Expenses related to obtaining building permits and registrations, if applicable.
    •    Replacement cost for affected structures is equivalent to the current market price for materials, labor,
         and other expenses related to obtaining building permits and registrations, if applicable.
(iv) Other cost and allowance: Interview local residents to determine
    •    Cost of excavation, relocation, reburial and other related costs
    •    Transportation costs for movable assets, including salvaged materials from original structures
(v) Price Comparison and Validation:
    •    Compare estimated replacement costs with the unit rates approved by the State Agency for
         Architecture, Construction, and Housing and Communal Services or other relevant bodies, if available.
    •    Consult with district- and AA-level authorities to verify and validate findings.
(vi) Cost Estimation and Reporting:
    •    Propose unit rates for compensation of affected assets (land, structures, perennial and annual crops)
         based on replacement cost principles and without depreciation in consultation with PMO and World
         Bank;
    •    Calculate the cost of compensation, assistance, and resettlement.

5.5 Public Consultations
     •   The consultant is required to conduct the following activities:
    •    Carrying out a series of public consultation meetings including one consultative meeting with local
         authorities and relevant agencies at district and AA levels and one meeting with potentially affected
         communities in each AA including host communities before the commencement of the IOL, SES, and
         RCS.
    •    The Project information to be shared and consulted with potentially affected people and communities
         includes, but not limited to:

    •    Project description and expected benefits of the Project;
    •    Potential land acquisition and resettlement impacts due to the reservoir area and WPZ;
    •    Feasible measures to minimize and mitigate the land acquisition and resettlement impacts;
    •    Proposed eligibility and entitlements for PAPs;
    •    Availability of replacement land;
    •    Restoration of loss of access to pasture land;
    •    Needs of PAPs in livelihood restoration and relocation preference;
    •    Schedules for the IOL, SES, and replacement cost survey;
    •    Mechanisms for continuing meaningful consultation with and participation of PAPs,
         community, and other stakeholders in land acquisition and resettlement planning,
         implementation, and monitoring; and
    •    Grievance redress mechanism.
    •    Consider as of inception the establishment of Community Resettlement Committees (CRC) at the level
         of each affected AA that will act throughout the land acquisition and resettlement planning process as
         negotiation instances between the Project and the Consultant on the one hand, and the community


                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

         on the other. Establishment and composition of the CRCs will be discussed with community leadership
         and local authorities. CRCs should be inclusive of all pertinent layers of the affected population,
         including youth, women and vulnerable groups. Establishing CRCs as the main negotiation and
         interaction avenue should not pre-empt other consultation avenues, including focus groups and
         general community meetings.
    •    Organizing public consultation meetings with PAPs and local authorities after completion of the IOL,
         SES, and RCS to present survey results, announced the cut-off date for eligibility for compensation,
         assistance, and resettlement, and discussed the proposed entitlements with PAPs and communities.
    •    Organizing public consultation meetings with PAPs and local authorities on the provisions of the draft
         LRRP2 before submission to World Bank for review and approval.
    •    Conducting in-depth interviews with key-informants (leaders of AA, village heads, Municipal
         Enterprises, District Agriculture Management , Department of Pastures and Breeding Livestock,
         Women’s Union) to obtain their insights about the Project’s impacts on local residents and LRP.
    •    Organizing FGDs with specific groups of PAPs (e.g., vulnerable households, winter pasture users,
         NTFP collectors, and groups of affected beekeepers) to understand their unique concerns,
         vulnerabilities, and recommendations.
These consultation activities should be held at a suitable time and place for women, and should also
take into account the needs of persons with disabilities (if any), as well as any barriers faced by
socially vulnerable groups, should also be considered when organizing such events. Whenever
possible, meetings should be held in neutral, accessible public spaces or within women-led civil
society organizations, where available.
All presentations must be delivered in the Kyrgyz language, and Project Information Booklets should
be distributed to all participants. All the concerns, suggestions, and recommendations raised by
meeting participants must be recorded and documented. This includes compiling attendance sheets
and photographic evidence of the consultations.
5.6 Livelihood Restoration Program (LRP)
As part of the LRRP2 preparation, the Consultant shall develop a comprehensive Livelihood
Restoration Program (LRP) for households and communities affected by the loss of pastures and
access to pastures and other productive resources due to the project. The development of the LRP
must adhere to the objectives, principles, and criteria outlined in the Project’s LRRF. The specific
requirements are as follows:
    •    Identify all eligible individuals/ households, including pasture users and vulnerable groups
         (e.g., low-income, elderly, disabled, women-headed households).
    •    Conduct participatory socio-economic assessments with affected households, with
         particular attention to vulnerable groups, to identify specific livelihood restoration needs,
         existing skills, and local economic opportunities.
    •    Assess the availability and condition of remaining pastures, including the updated pasture
         capacity data provided in the Pasture Report, and access routes.
    •    Consult affected households and relevant agencies on preference for restoration strategies,
         including pasture replacement, vocational training, market studies for local employment, or
         enterprise development.
    •    Propose viable and locally appropriate livelihood restoration measures tailored to each Aiyl
         Aimak, referencing preliminary options in LRRF. The initial income restoration measures
         include enhancing strengthening winter fodder supply, establishing a revolving fund to
         support agricultural loans, offering vocational training programs (e.g., pasture use, animal
         husbandry), promoting meat breeds of cattle and horses, supporting the development of
         goat and yak farming, and providing training related to construction activities.



                                                                                                                    Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement Framework

    •    Identify replacement pastures based on slope, carrying capacity, and current use in
         consultation with District Agriculture Management Departments, Departments of Pastures
         and Breeding Livestock, Aiyl Okmotus, and Municipal Enterprises, and outline the process
         for formal allocation.
    •    Update proposals for restoring access to currently used pastures that will become
         inaccessible, including road and bridge infrastructure. Carry out consultations with affected
         communities to confirm infrastructure proposals listed in the Pasture Report for the
         replacement or restoration of these assets and infrastructure, in accordance with the
         provisions outlined in the LRRF.
    •    Coordinate with relevant government bodies to address unresolved land allocation and
         jurisdiction issues.
    •    Coordinate with government programs, local authorities, and NGOs to integrate LRP
         activities with ongoing development initiatives.
    •    Estimate detailed LRP implementation costs, including inputs, infrastructure, training, and
         monitoring.
    •    Define institutional roles and responsibilities for LRP implementation, including national and
         local agencies, community organizations, and external support services.
    •    Develop a robust M&E framework with indicators to measure LRP effectiveness in restoring
         household income and living standards.
5.7 Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM)
The grievance redress mechanism (GRM) shall be developed in accordance with the Project’s
Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP) and the LRRF, and the WB’s ESS10. In particular, the GRM will
be developed based on current ongoing GRM practices that have been applied locally as per
national laws and regulations and their design takes into account the views of affected communities
expressed during the LRRP2 preparation. Particular attention will be given to ensuring the GRM is
accessible, inclusive, and responsive, with specific provisions to facilitate access for disadvantaged
and vulnerable individuals or groups.
5.8 Special Considerations for the Needs of Women
All transactions related to physical or economic displacement require particular attention to gender.
For example:
    •    Intra-household analysis may be needed where women’s and men’s livelihoods are affected
         differently.
    •    Women’s and men’s preferences in terms of compensation mechanisms, such as replacement land or
         alternative access to natural resources rather than in cash, should be explored
    •    Documentation of ownership or occupancy and compensation payments should be issued in the name
         of both spouses or single heads of households
    •    Proposed land acquisition, resettlement, and livelihood restoration measures, such as skills training,
         job opportunities etc., should be equally available to women and adapted to their needs
    •    The consultation process should ensure that women’s perspectives are obtained, and their interests
         factored in.

The consultant shall submit the following reports:
    •    Inception Report: This report will present the methodology, resources, tools, and detailed schedule
         for delivering the assignment’s objectives and scope of work. It will include a detailed outline of the
         LRRP2 structure, in accordance with the Project's LRRF and the World Bank’s ESS 5 and other

           international standards. Additionally, it also includes the update of the screening report will be also

           Bank and other Lenders for approval within one (1) week of contract signing.
      •    Draft LRRP: This report will cover the full scope of work outlined in the TOR and will be prepared
           following comprehensive stakeholder engagement and consultation. The draft LRRP2 will be
           submitted to K1-PMO, the World Bank and other Lenders for review within nine (9) weeks of contract
           signing.

           other Lenders ensuring all review comments are addressed and will be submitted within eleven (11)
           weeks of contract signing.

           consultation meetings, FGDs, and KIIs.
•       All deliverables must be submitted in English and Kyrgyz in both editable (Word, Excel, etc.) and PDF
formats.

7. Qualification and Experience of the Consultant
The consulting firm must demonstrate substantial experience and technical capacity in the
preparation of Resettlement Plans, or other land acquisition and resettlement-related documents in
accordance with international standards, particularly the World Bank’s ESF and ESS5. The firm should
have at least seven (7) years of proven experience in implementing or supporting involuntary
resettlement and livelihood restoration activities in infrastructure, energy, or similar sectors,
preferably for projects financed by multilateral development banks such as the World Bank, ADB, or
EBRD. The firm must demonstrate a track record of effectively conducting socio-economic surveys,
meaningful consultations with affected persons (including vulnerable groups), and stakeholder
engagement in compliance with the principles of transparency, inclusiveness, and free, prior, and
informed participation. Familiarity with the national legal and institutional framework for land
acquisition and resettlement in the Kyrgyz Republic is highly desirable. The firm must also
demonstrate the ability to coordinate with government agencies, manage multidisciplinary teams,
and deliver high-quality, timely reports.

                                         •   Proficiency in GIS software, relational database systems, and data analysis
                                             tools.
                                         •   Experience in supervising field teams for data entry, cleaning, validation,
                                             and quality control.
                                         •   Excellent communication skills and ability to provide training and technical
                                             support to other team members and the Client on database use.
 Local field enumerators/encoders        •   Experience in household surveys, local consultations, and data collection.
                                         •   Skilled in using GIS tools to support the IOL.
                                         •   Fluent in Kyrgyz.


8. Support to be provided by the Client
The below supports will be provided by the Client to the Consultant for preparing the LRRP2:
    •    Share all relevant project documentation, including but not limited to the Feasibility Study Report,
         ESIA report, and the LRRF of the Project.
    •    Maps (and relevant drawings, if any) on the project design, including the location of construction
         sites, associated facilities, and other project-affected areas.
    •    Assist the Consultant in logistical arrangements for fieldwork, including providing letters of
         introduction, arranging meetings, field visits, and consultations with relevant stakeholders.
    •    Support and supervision of the Resettlement Specialist under K1-PMO.
